<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-985987057371463751 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=985987057371463751><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title="Deleted User">Deleted User</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'985986223191523378')"> How otherwise you handle multi-petabyte processing? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 13, 2022 4:20 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-985987057371463751>6/13/2022 4:20 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Extremely few use cases for multi-petabyte processing. And there are tools for it, but it&#39;s <strong>extremely</strong> few use cases. I worked with a data warehouse that had a petabyte of data for the last couple of years and there are many many tricks you can do that make more monetary sense than hitting things with a very large cluster.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-985987350695936110 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=985987350695936110><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title="Deleted User" data-user-id=456226577798135808>Deleted User</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 13, 2022 4:21 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-985987350695936110>6/13/2022 4:21 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Which tools? I know only two mature - Hadoop and Spark</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-985987895364026388 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=985987895364026388><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/499104423872823298/1a01884db1516a1f0a2fa9a48ed24947.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=winenose data-user-id=499104423872823298>Lauri</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 13, 2022 4:23 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-985987895364026388>6/13/2022 4:23 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t mean tools, I mean techniques that work around the need to work with a petabyte of data at the same time. Things like partitioning, transforming stuff in smaller batches, aggregating as things come in, etc. All the way down to actually saving the data in a smaller format so that the information-per-byte ratio is better.

A petabyte of CSV compared to a petabyte of Parquet has a very different amount of actual information in it</span></div></div></div></div></div>

    loading="lazy"
    class="chatlog__emoji "
    alt="🙂"
    title="slight_smile"
    src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f642.svg">
The stuff that companies share at their main conferences is definitely in the &quot;overpromise and under-deliver&quot; section.
&quot;Coming soon&quot; at best means that they&#39;ll announce general availability the next day, which is cool.
Usually it means that a product manager has thought of it and put it into an internal roadmap presentation under &quot;maybe in future&quot;.
And sometimes it&#39;s just meant to trigger the competition to expend resources trying to tackle a very hard problem to achieve an imagined feature parity while the announcing company has no plans to ever go down that road.

With any such announcements it&#39;s best to expect absolutely nothing to actually materialize and just appreciate the effort that was put into marketing.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

What I would do is instrument the current setup that runs every minute, run it for a couple of days and see how well it does. My guess is that it&#39;ll peak at around 10 second run duration with a very long and fat tail</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-986775381854019634 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=986775381854019634><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/255309049195790336/d18a15367c57e51f757d896c542ff332.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=hypnosisfuca data-user-id=255309049195790336>Arpan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, June 15, 2022 8:33 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-986775381854019634>6/15/2022 8:33 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The modern data stack (MDS) is a suite of tools used for data integration. These tools include, in order of how the data flows:

a fully managed ELT data pipeline
a cloud-based columnar warehouse or data lake as a destination
a data transformation tool

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-988296636516139009 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=988296636516139009><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 20, 2022 1:17 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-988296636516139009>6/20/2022 1:17 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>In terms of ETL / ELT, you have various areas of concern. Landing the data from the source into your warehouse / lake is generally the first one.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-988296912488775730 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=988296912488775730><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, June 20, 2022 1:19 AM">1:19 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Fivetran and the like work great for simple data movement for common sources and sinks. But you pay for the convenience. I think most / all of the popular tools are volume-based, so they can get expensive quickly.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-988297489285279786 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=988297489285279786><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, June 20, 2022 1:21 AM">1:21 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Once your data is actually in your warehouse, probably with some metadata (loaded timestamp, data source), you may have extra &quot;stuff&quot; to do to it to generate business value. Maybe that&#39;s performing additional data modeling to make it easier for your analysts to use. Or maybe your DS have built ML models to process the data and generate a prediction. Whatever goes into that logic is generally mostly custom to your needs.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Many times, myself included, I&#39;ve seen folks want to rebuild a ticketing system, or hand-roll a dashboard system with something like D3.js. 

It&#39;s a fools errand. Companies invest large teams in building off the shelf teams. In house apps usually will never receive the service they need to be comparable in a significant way. 

But I&#39;m sure a more narrow use case could justify maintaining your own code base.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-988974762376196116 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=988974762376196116><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=pybokeh data-user-id=577284407879139338>pybokeh</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, June 21, 2022 10:12 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-988974762376196116>6/21/2022 10:12 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hello!  I am new here!  I used to be a data engineer a few years ago.  Now I am a technical product owner of a data product.  My product relies on data supplied by 3rd party data provider which my product then sells at a higher price to its customers.  My product that I am developing will be delivered through an API where the data will be sourced by 2 to 3 data providers.  The standard or custom response my product supplies to the client is comprised of data from the 2 or 3 data providers whose data and/or data format is different between them - oh so much fun!  NOT!  So among many challenges and things I have to do, one thing I have do is compare my product&#39;s response data to the equivalent response data of my data providers.  So basically, I am having to compare 2 sets of JSON data sets and validating that values in my product&#39;s response data should contain values provided by the data provider.  Curious if anyone has had experience doing this before?  Is there a magical tool that does this bulk comparison of JSON data sets or is inevitable that I or someone has to create custom code to do this comparison?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-988978608657797190 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=988978608657797190><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=pybokeh data-user-id=577284407879139338>pybokeh</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, June 21, 2022 10:27 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-988978608657797190>6/21/2022 10:27 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>What I have done so far.  I have saved or stored the raw JSON files that came from our 3rd party vendor onto our Snowflake staging.  Then created a single variant column table containing the JSON data from the JSON files.   I then used Snowflake&#39;s flatten() function to normalize the responses contained in the variant column into final tables.  I then repeat this with my product&#39;s JSON response files.  Then I compare the 2 sets.  The problem with this is there are complex business rules akin to like IF-ELSE statements.  Something along the lines of: if this value is in this response node, then do this, if it is not found in this response node, look at this other response node, etc.  Trying to duplicate or translate this type of logic in the realm of normalized relational tables seem unnatural to me.  So now I&#39;m thinking, perhaps I need to create Python code at the low level data structure (key: value) like its dictionary data structure in conjunction with the json module.  After creating some initial code for doing this, it is starting to get hairy.  Basically, my code will take 2 inputs: one directory path containing raw JSON files from the 3rd party vendor and another directory path containing the JSON files from my product&#39;s API.  Then it will loop through the JSON files and compare on the fly.  I don&#39;t know if this is the route I should commit to.

EDIT: Basically I am on the fence on whether to try to do this comparison somehow within Snowflake environment + Python code or do this comparison completely outside of Snowflake (ie. not create the normalized data sets, but compare using low level Python data structure using looping, JSON module, Python dict, etc).</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, June 21, 2022 10:44 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-989027718836412430 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989027718836412430><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=pybokeh>pybokeh</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'988978608657797190')"> What I have done so far.  I have saved or stored the raw JSON files that came from our 3rd party vendor onto our Snowflake staging.  Then created a single variant column table containing the JSON data from the JSON files.   I then used Snowflake&#39;s flatten() function to normalize the responses contained in the variant column into final tables.  I then repeat this with my product&#39;s JSON response files.  Then I compare the 2 sets.  The problem with this is there are complex business rules akin to like IF-ELSE statements.  Something along the lines of: if this value is in this response node, then do this, if it is not found in this response node, look at this other response node, etc.  Trying to duplicate or translate this type of logic in the realm of normalized relational tables seem unnatural to me.  So now I&#39;m thinking, perhaps I need to create Python code at the low level data structure (key: value) like its dictionary data structure in conjunction with the json module.  After creating some initial code for doing this, it is starting to get hairy.  Basically, my code will take 2 inputs: one directory path containing raw JSON files from the 3rd party vendor and another directory path containing the JSON files from my product&#39;s API.  Then it will loop through the JSON files and compare on the fly.  I don&#39;t know if this is the route I should commit to.

EDIT: Basically I am on the fence on whether to try to do this comparison somehow within Snowflake environment + Python code or do this comparison completely outside of Snowflake (ie. not create the normalized data sets, but compare using low level Python data structure using looping, JSON module, Python dict, etc). </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, June 21, 2022 10:44 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, June 22, 2022 1:43 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-989027718836412430>6/22/2022 1:43 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Could you meet in the middle and just prepare SQL in Python and execute it against the DB? I don’t know the volume of data you’re dealing with but if it’s anything particularly large you’ll probably save yourself a lot of headaches if you can leverage Snowflake for compute instead</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989028013817610271 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989028013817610271><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 22, 2022 1:44 AM">1:44 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>There’s frameworks/products like dbt, great expectations, and datafold that might be worth exploring, but I’m not sure of your exact use-case, and they may not be flexible enough for you</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

Overall, the model is quite flexible for extension and encourages establishing proper relationships between data and does a good job of discouraging data duplication. The major downsides are that the join infrastructure often gets out of hand quickly and intermediate table / view structures need to be generated to improve performance. The data vault structure is practically unusable for anyone besides someone with fairly good sql experience but can make the data engineer&#39;s life easier for helping to generate data products.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989361686903410698 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989361686903410698><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 22, 2022 11:50 PM">11:50 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think DV is good option if you&#39;re prepared to automate a lot of the explicit and implicit requirements, as recommended in the data vault book, but it feels like a trap if you don&#39;t understand the extra requirements to deploy it properly.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989362093251776562 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989362093251776562><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 22, 2022 11:51 PM">11:51 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Also, I think starting out with data vault can hinder you from initially delivering value because of the extra modeling and automation required to utilize it.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989363010709647360 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989363010709647360><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 22, 2022 11:55 PM">11:55 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It feels like &quot;too much&quot; when you&#39;re starting and often can feel &quot;too late&quot; if you start using it later.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989364210205085737 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989364210205085737><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:00 AM">12:00 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Overall, I am happy that we&#39;re using it but it&#39;s something that pays for itself over time and it&#39;s not necessarily evident that following such a methodology would immediately bring end user value.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

Found it any good? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=maciam data-user-id=177473204011401216>Mac</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 11:31 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-989538288937365614>6/23/2022 11:31 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Never used, but what I’ve heard positives regarding use, negatives regarding price</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989538646086545438 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989538646086545438><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 11:33 AM">11:33 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><strong>Question of the Day</strong>
What are some things you want product/product engineering to consider prior to building a new feature regarding future analytics?</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 11:33 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-989544268634927114 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989544268634927114><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/493193412045176843/180ce3b2d099537151e2bc4130a018cc.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/252313646682734595/eca0565bddbb2a0cf78752b7b374cb0d.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=zachary42>Zachary</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'989361173839368232')"> I&#39;ve used it to model parts of our Azure database. Overall, the model is quite flexible for extension and encourages establishing proper relationships between data and does a good job of discouraging data duplication. The major downsides are that the join infrastructure often gets out of hand quickly and intermediate table / view structures need to be generated to improve performance. The data vault structure is practically unusable for anyone besides someone with fairly good sql experience but can make the data engineer&#39;s life easier for helping to generate data products. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=jacocal data-user-id=493193412045176843>Jaco</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 11:55 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-989544268634927114>6/23/2022 11:55 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Thank you so much for this answer Zachary! It was very insightful. I have a few questions:
1. When do you consider it was the right timing to migrate from Kimball to Data Vault?
2. How do you manage &quot;data as time&quot; within your architecture?
3. If allowed to, which services are you using in Azure for the architecture? (My guess would be SQL, Cosmos and Synapse)
4. How do Links manage the information delivery?
5. Are Hubs keys auto filled by the Satellites?
6. For complexity, have you tried reducing from DV to Star schema on a DWH -&gt; Data Mart delivery? If yes, how was your experience?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-989553607554764801 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989553607554764801><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/252313646682734595/eca0565bddbb2a0cf78752b7b374cb0d.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=zachary42 data-user-id=252313646682734595>Zachary</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:32 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-989553607554764801>6/23/2022 12:32 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Data vault is good for wrangling in business key relationships and I would primarily advise migrating towards it when it feels like you&#39;re in need for join and key standardization. Once the structure is set up I have some more confidence that the report tables that are being generated actually are based on proper transaction relationships.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989554575419789392 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989554575419789392><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:36 PM">12:36 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s hard to say exactly when because it depends upon how much confidence the other departments have in the data team. A lot of data teams are a bit of a disaster where reliability is shaky and new changes to data team roster necessitate proof of deliverable value. If you&#39;re scrambling to show a brighter future then data vault can&#39;t deliver that in a timely manner.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989555066979622952 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989555066979622952><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:38 PM">12:38 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>You use Kimball alongside data vault. Data vault is the storage and standardization platform and Kimball is still used for data delivery to users.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989555278456451152 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989555278456451152><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:39 PM">12:39 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t understand what you mean by &quot;data as time&quot;, could you clarify?</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989555938925101077 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989555938925101077><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:42 PM">12:42 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We use ADLS for as a persistent staging area, cosmos for some operational / real-time reporting, and Azure sql db hyperscale for dwh / data reporting.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989556364638584872 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989556364638584872><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:43 PM">12:43 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>My company doesn&#39;t have enough data or have as much of a need for mpp queries so synapse doesn&#39;t deliver much value.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989556572218855484 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989556572218855484><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:44 PM">12:44 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The entire database is like 60b records so not really big data per say.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989557637291053066 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989557637291053066><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:48 PM">12:48 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Satellites off of hubs trend towards dimensions and satellites off of links trend toward facts. You use the data vault structure to build the star schema structure and rebuild it as necessary.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989558027080318996 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989558027080318996><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:50 PM">12:50 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Fact and dimension tables are virtualize off of the data vault / business vault layer and may be materialized or loaded into a physical table if needed.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989559168061034576 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989559168061034576><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:54 PM">12:54 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>A lot of my end users prefer versatile report tables over star schemas so I trend towards that direction. Overall transformation from DV to star schema is conceptually straightforward; though, you&#39;ll often be put into a position where you will need to build bridge tables to deal with reports that pass through several link tables.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989560292348420106 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989560292348420106><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 12:59 PM">12:59 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hubs are filled from staging tables. You generate hash key and hash diff columns that are used to help load the hubs, links, and satellites.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989561203057623050 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989561203057623050><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 1:02 PM">1:02 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>With data vault you&#39;re enforcing a standard that grants you extensibility and a layer that helps you generate and rebuild reporting infrastructure. You pay for it by requiring an additional layer of abstraction and having to pay the tolls of having a highly normalized data layer that needs some additional labor to make joins performant.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-989561868861464656 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=989561868861464656><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 23, 2022 1:05 PM">1:05 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>In this sense some businesses may not find the juice worth the squeeze. Personally, I&#39;ve found it helpful for our business but don&#39;t agree with the evangelists that say it&#39;s right for all businesses.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-990318307775225926 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=990318307775225926><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, June 25, 2022 3:11 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-990318307775225926>6/25/2022 3:11 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>my 2 cents on glue:

<strong>Glue catalog</strong> - Good and functional as a serverless hive metastore - minus the limitations of no table renaming and 100 partitions per request. Spark integration is there. Partition indexes are neat. Web UI sucks
<strong>Glue jobs</strong> - meh. It works, but it&#39;s slow and the runtimes update at a glacial pace. the glue specific internals (dynamic frame, bookmarks) are poorly documented
<strong>Glue crawlers</strong> - slow, expensive, and i see a lot of crap online of like &quot;run this crawler over your 900GB of data to discover today&#39;s 1 new hive partition&quot;. best avoided
<strong>Glue interactive sessions</strong> - <em>okay</em>, but no dynamic allocation sucks. you set your workers and that&#39;s it. they are also very expensive</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, June 25, 2022 3:13 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-990318360032059453 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=990318360032059453><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, June 25, 2022 3:11 PM">3:11 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>i have no experience with the schema registry</span></div></div></div></div></div>

As far as I can tell, a data cube has three actual manifestations: 

As a list of dimensional combinations and a count of their occurrences (store a, part b: 100). 

As a specific data structure in an OLAP system that can be queried with a special syntax to drill, roundup, slice, and pivot the data. 

And finally, simply as a physical star-schema or snowflake schema set up in a RDMS.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-990664876315787324 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=990664876315787324><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, June 26, 2022 2:08 PM">2:08 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Am I missing something?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-993334772929667082 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=993334772929667082><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, July 3, 2022 10:57 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-993334772929667082>7/3/2022 10:57 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Yeah my point was more that SQL is inherently a language of a lot of different things chained together. Your average query in an OLAP or OLTP system might have a where clause, a join, maybe a group by (less so for OLTP probably) so it’s sort of inherently not an atomic operation, and therefore harder to cover with a unit test. You can break that query apart into atomic pieces for sure, but you’re more than likely going to pay a significant price in performance for that. 

I don’t really mean like data tests i.e. what dbt or great expectations give you.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
